# Data Flow Q&A: Envoy Request Routing

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/envoy--d7809ba2 (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Task Type:** Data Flow Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Envoy is a high-performance proxy that routes HTTP requests from downstream clients to upstream services. Understanding the complete path from the initial TCP accept through filter processing to the final upstream connection is critical for working with Envoy's architecture.

## Task

Trace the complete path of a single HTTP request from the moment a downstream client TCP connection is accepted through filter chain processing, route resolution, upstream cluster selection, and connection establishment. Identify every key transformation point, component boundary crossing, and state change.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Envoy's request routing flow:

### Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

When a downstream client establishes a TCP connection to Envoy, how does the request travel from socket accept to network filter processing?

- Which component accepts the incoming TCP connection?
- How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?
- At what point does the connection get handed to the HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)?
- What triggers the initial `onData()` call when bytes arrive?

### Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration

Once bytes arrive at the HCM, how does Envoy parse HTTP and iterate through filters?

- How does the codec parse the byte stream into HTTP headers/body?
- When is the `ActiveStream` created and how does it relate to filter iteration?
- How does the `FilterManager` determine the order of decoder filter execution?
- What filter return values can stop or continue iteration?

### Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection

When the router filter is invoked, how does it select the upstream destination?

- How does the router determine which route configuration to use?
- What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?
- How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?
- What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?

### Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow

Once an upstream host is selected, how does Envoy establish the connection and forward the request?

- How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?
- What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?
- How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?
- At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

```
# Envoy Request Routing Flow

## Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Evidence
<consolidated list of supporting file paths and line references>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Cite specific files, classes, and methods — avoid vague or speculative answers
- Focus on the core request path, not error handling or edge cases
- Trace a single successful HTTP/1.1 request without TLS termination

The investigation document has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here is a summary of the findings:

---

## Envoy Request Routing Flow — Summary

### Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

1. **Socket accept**: `TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()` (`tcp_listener_impl.cc:56`) is triggered by a level-triggered read event registered on the listening socket. It calls `ioHandle().accept()` to extract the peer socket and wraps it in `AcceptedSocketImpl`.

2. **Handoff to `ActiveTcpListener`**: `TcpListenerImpl` calls `cb_.onAccept()`, which dispatches to `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` (`active_tcp_listener.cc:80`) → `onAcceptWorker()` → creates `ActiveTcpSocket`.

3. **Listener filter chain**: `ActiveStreamListenerBase::onSocketAccepted()` (`active_stream_listener_base.h:85`) calls `createListenerFilterChain()` + `startFilterChain()`. Listener filters (e.g., HTTP Inspector, Original Destination) run to detect the transport protocol and other properties for filter chain matching.

4. **Network filter chain selection**: After all listener filters complete, `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` (`active_tcp_socket.cc:185`) calls `listener_.newConnection()`. Inside `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (`active_stream_listener_base.cc:38`), `filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info)` selects the matching network filter chain based on connection properties.

5. **HCM instantiation**: `createNetworkFilterChain(*server_conn_ptr, filter_chain->networkFilterFactories())` instantiates the HCM (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) as a `Network::ReadFilter`.

6. **`onData()` trigger**: When bytes arrive on the connection, the dispatcher fires a read event → `ConnectionImpl::onRead()` → `ReadFilterManager::onRead()` → `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()` (`conn_
... (truncated)

During construction, it registers a level-triggered file event on the listening socket:\n\n```cpp\nsocket_->ioHandle().initializeFileEvent(\n    dispatcher, [this](uint32_t events) { return onSocketEvent(events); },\n    Event::FileTriggerType::Level, Event::FileReadyType::Read);\n```\n\nWhen the event fires, `TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()` (tcp_listener_impl.cc:56) calls `socket_->ioHandle().accept()` to extract the peer socket, then wraps it in an `AcceptedSocketImpl` and calls `cb_.onAccept(std::make_unique<AcceptedSocketImpl>(...))` (tcp_listener_impl.cc:117).\n\nThe callback target is `ActiveTcpListener` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.h), which implements `Network::TcpListenerCallbacks`.\n\n### How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?\n\nAfter all listener filters run (see below), `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc:185) calls `listener_.newConnection(std::move(socket_), std::move(stream_info_))`.\n\nInside `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:38-76):\n\n```cpp\nconst auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);\n```\n\n`findFilterChain()` matches against configured criteria such as destination IP/port, server name (SNI), transport protocol (set by the TLS inspector listener filter), and application protocol (set by the HTTP Inspector listener filter). The matching is hierarchical and the most-specific match wins.\n\n### At what point does the connection get handed to the HCM?\n\nStill inside `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (active_stream_listener_base.cc:58-75), once a filter chain is found:\n\n1. A transport socket is created: `filter_chain->transportSocketFactory().createDownstreamTransportSocket()`\n2. The network filter chain is instantiated via: `config_->filterChainFactory().createNetworkFilterChain(*server_conn_ptr, filter_chain->networkFilterFactories())`\n\nThe HCM (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) is added as a `Network::ReadFilter` during step 3. `ConnectionManagerImpl` implements `Network::ReadFilter` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h:61).\n\n### What triggers the initial `onData()` call when bytes arrive?\n\nAfter the server connection is created, the underlying `ConnectionImpl` registers a read event on the socket. When bytes arrive, the dispatcher fires the read-ready callback, which drains data into a buffer and calls `ReadFilterManager::onRead()` \u2014 iterating through each `Network::ReadFilter` in the network filter chain, eventually calling `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool)` (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:486).\n\n### Summary of the accept path:\n\n```\nsocket read event\n  \u2192 TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()               [tcp_listener_impl.cc:56]\n    \u2192 ioHandle.accept() \u2192 AcceptedSocketImpl\n    \u2192 cb_.onAccept()\n  \u2192 ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()                  [active_tcp_listener.cc:80]\n    \u2192 onAcceptWorker()                              [active_tcp_listener.cc:108]\n      \u2192 make_unique<ActiveTcpSocket>\n      \u2192 onSocketAccepted()                          [active_stream_listener_base.h:85]\n        \u2192 createListenerFilterChain() + startFilterChain()\n        \u2192 [listener filters run: e.g., Original Dst, HTTP Inspector]\n        \u2192 ActiveTcpSocket::continueFilterChain()    [active_tcp_socket.cc:111]\n          \u2192 newConnection()                         [active_tcp_socket.cc:185]\n  \u2192 ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()       [active_stream_listener_base.cc:38]\n    \u2192 filterChainManager().findFilterChain()        (selects network filter chain)\n    \u2192 createServerConnection()\n    \u2192 createNetworkFilterChain()                    (instantiates HCM as ReadFilter)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration\n\n### How does the codec parse the byte stream into HTTP headers/body?\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()` (conn_manager_impl.cc:486) lazily creates the codec on first call:\n\n```cpp\ncreateCodec(data);  // conn_manager_impl.cc:496\n```\n\n`createCodec()` calls `config_->createCodec(read_callbacks_->connection(), data, *this, overload_manager_)` which inspects the byte stream to determine HTTP version and constructs the appropriate codec (HTTP/1.1: `ServerConnectionImpl`, HTTP/2: `Http2::ServerConnectionImpl`).\n\nThen `onData()` calls `codec_->dispatch(data)` in a loop.\n\nFor HTTP/1.1, `ServerConnectionImpl::dispatch()` (http1/codec_impl.cc:1298) calls the base `ConnectionImpl::dispatch()` which feeds bytes to `llhttp`/`http_parser`. As parsing progresses:\n\n- **`onMessageBeginBase()`** (codec_impl.cc:1266): creates an `ActiveRequest` and calls `callbacks_.newStream(active_request_->response_encoder_)` \u2014 this is the `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` call that creates the `ActiveStream`.\n- **`onHeadersCompleteBase()`** (codec_impl.cc:1199): if the request has a body (chunked or content-length > 0), immediately calls `active_request_->request_decoder_->decodeHeaders(std::move(headers), false)`. Otherwise, defers until `onMessageCompleteBase()` with `end_stream=true`.\n- **`onBody()`** (codec_impl.cc:1290): calls `request_decoder_->decodeData(data, false)`.\n- **`onMessageCompleteBase()`** (codec_impl.cc:1325): calls `decodeHeaders(..., true)` (if deferred) or `decodeData(buffer, true)` to signal end of stream.\n\n### When is the `ActiveStream` created and how does it relate to filter iteration?\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` (conn_manager_impl.cc:387) is called by the codec when the HTTP message begins. It allocates a new `ActiveStream`, wires it to the `ResponseEncoder`, and prepends it to `streams_`.\n\n`ActiveStream`'s constructor (conn_manager_impl.cc:812-929) creates the `FilterManager` and starts idle/request timers.\n\nThe `ActiveStream` implements `RequestDecoder` \u2014 the codec calls `decodeHeaders()`/`decodeData()`/`decodeTrailers()` on it. `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` (conn_manager_impl.cc:1193) then drives filter chain iteration.\n\n### How does the `FilterManager` determine the order of decoder filter execution?\n\nIn `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` (conn_manager_impl.cc:1402):\n\n```cpp\nfilter_manager_.createDownstreamFilterChain();\n```\n\nThis calls `config_->filterFactory()` to invoke each configured filter factory callback, which calls `FilterManager::addStreamDecoderFilter()` / `addStreamEncoderFilter()` / `addStreamFilter()` in the order they are configured. Decoder filters are stored in `decoder_filters_` in configuration order.\n\nThen `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders(*request_headers_, end_stream)` (conn_manager_impl.cc:1439) is called, which dispatches to `FilterManager::decodeHeaders(nullptr, headers, end_stream)` (filter_manager.cc:537).\n\n`FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` iterates `decoder_filters_` from front to back (configuration order):\n\n```cpp\nfor (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    FilterHeadersStatus status = (*entry)->decodeHeaders(headers, (*entry)->end_stream_);\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n### What filter return values can stop or continue iteration?\n\nDecoder filter `decodeHeaders()` returns `FilterHeadersStatus`:\n\n| Return Value | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| `Continue` | Advance to the next decoder filter |\n| `StopIteration` | Stop; the filter must call `continueDecoding()` later to resume from the next filter |\n| `StopAllIterationAndBuffer` | Stop and buffer all subsequent data frames |\n| `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` | Stop and apply watermark-based buffering |\n| `ContinueAndDontEndStream` | Continue but suppress the `end_stream` flag to subsequent filters |\n\nHandled in `ActiveStreamFilterBase::commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback()` (filter_manager.cc:130). If `stoppedAll()` is true, iteration halts and resumes via `commonContinue()` (filter_manager.cc:50) when the filter calls `continueDecoding()`.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection\n\n### How does the router determine which route configuration to use?\n\nBefore calling `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders()`, `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` (conn_manager_impl.cc:1233-1244) snaps the route configuration:\n\n```cpp\nsnapped_route_config_ = connection_manager_.config_->routeConfigProvider()->configCast();\n```\n\nThis is an atomic snapshot of the current `RouteConfiguration` proto derived from static config or RDS. The `snapped_route_config_` is stored on the `ActiveStream` and passed to `refreshCachedRoute()` which calls `snapped_route_config_->route(request_headers, stream_info, random)`.\n\n### What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?\n\nInside the router filter `Filter::decodeHeaders()` (source/common/router/router.cc:445):\n\n1. `callbacks_->route()` returns the cached route (set earlier by `refreshCachedRoute()` in the HCM). The route config's `RouteImpl::matches()` evaluated all prefix/header/path matchers against the request.\n2. `route_->routeEntry()` returns the `RouteEntry` which holds the cluster name, timeout, retry policy, etc.\n3. `config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName())` (router.cc:519) fetches the `ThreadLocalCluster` from the cluster manager by name. Returns null if cluster does not exist (\u2192 503).\n4. `cluster_ = cluster->info()` stores the cluster's static metadata.\n\n### How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?\n\n```cpp\nauto host_selection_response = cluster->chooseHost(this);  // router.cc:664\n```\n\n`chooseHost()` delegates to the cluster's load balancer (Round Robin, Least Request, Random, Ring Hash, etc.). In the common synchronous path (no async host selection), it immediately returns a `HostConstSharedPtr`. If the returned host is null, `sendNoHealthyUpstreamResponse()` sends a 503.\n\n### What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?\n\nWith a valid host, `continueDecodeHeaders()` (router.cc:714) calls:\n\n```cpp\nstd::unique_ptr<GenericConnPool> generic_conn_pool = createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host);\n```\n\nThen an `UpstreamRequest` is created (router.cc:845) and immediately calls:\n\n```cpp\nconn_pool_->newStream(this);  // upstream_request.cc:404\n```\n\n`HttpConnPoolImplBase::newStream()` (conn_pool_base.cc:59-65) calls `newStreamImpl()` which:\n- If a ready (idle) client exists: attaches the stream immediately and fires `onPoolReady`.\n- Otherwise: creates a new TCP connection to the upstream host (via `ConnPoolImplBase::tryCreateNewConnections()`), queues the request as pending, and fires `onPoolReady` when the connection is established.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow\n\n### How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?\n\n`ConnPoolImplBase` (the base of all connection pools) manages three client lists: `ready_clients_`, `busy_clients_`, and `connecting_clients_`. When `newStreamImpl()` is called:\n\n1. If `ready_clients_` is non-empty, an idle client is taken and the stream is attached immediately via `attachStreamToClient()` \u2192 `onPoolReady()`.\n2. If no ready client exists, `tryCreateNewConnections()` initiates a new TCP connection to the upstream, creating a `CodecClient` (HTTP/1.1) or a multiplexed client (HTTP/2). The `PendingStream` is enqueued.\n3. When the TCP connection completes and the codec is initialized, the client moves to `ready_clients_` and the queued `PendingStream` is dispatched via `onPoolReady()`.\n\n`HttpConnPoolImplBase::onPoolReady()` (conn_pool_base.cc:84-93) calls:\n```cpp\nHttp::RequestEncoder& new_encoder = http_client->newStreamEncoder(response_decoder);\ncallbacks.onPoolReady(new_encoder, ...);\n```\n\nThis calls `UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady()` (upstream_request.cc:584), which stores `upstream_` (the `GenericUpstream`/`RequestEncoder`) and records connection timing in `StreamInfo`.\n\n### What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?\n\nThe last filter in the upstream HTTP filter chain is `UpstreamCodecFilter` (source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.cc). It is the terminal filter added by `DefaultUpstreamHttpFilterChainFactory` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:251-272).\n\nWhen headers have been processed by upstream filters, `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:52) is called:\n\n```cpp\nconst Http::Status status =\n    callbacks_->upstreamCallbacks()->upstream()->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n```\n\nFor HTTP/1.1, `upstream()` is a `Http1::RequestEncoderImpl` whose `encodeHeaders()` serializes the HTTP/1.1 request line and headers into a `Buffer` and writes to the upstream `Connection`.\n\nBody data follows via `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeData()` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:97) \u2192 `upstream()->encodeData()`.\n\nIf `onPoolReady` has not yet fired when `acceptHeadersFromRouter()` is called, `UpstreamCodecFilter` latches the headers in `latched_headers_` and waits. On `onUpstreamConnectionEstablished()` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:40), it replays `decodeHeaders()`.\n\n### How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?\n\nWhen the upstream sends a response, the upstream `CodecClient` (wrapping the upstream TCP connection) parses bytes using `ClientConnectionImpl`. The parsed response is delivered to `UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge` (the `ResponseDecoder` passed to `newStreamEncoder()`):\n\n- **`CodecBridge::decodeHeaders()`** (upstream_codec_filter.cc:147): calls `filter_.callbacks_->encodeHeaders(std::move(headers), end_stream, ...)` \u2014 this invokes `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` on the *downstream* filter manager, starting the encoder filter chain.\n- **`CodecBridge::decodeData()`** (upstream_codec_filter.cc:194): calls `filter_.callbacks_->encodeData(data, end_stream)` \u2192 `FilterManager::encodeData()`.\n- **`CodecBridge::decodeTrailers()`** (upstream_codec_filter.cc:200): calls `filter_.callbacks_->encodeTrailers()`.\n\n`FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (filter_manager.cc:1225) iterates `encoder_filters_` in front-to-back order (which corresponds to reverse configuration order, since encoder filters are prepended). Each filter gets to modify or stop the response. After all encoder filters pass, the response is written to the downstream socket via:\n\n```cpp\nfilter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders(headers, modified_end_stream);  // filter_manager.cc:1305\n```\n\n`filter_manager_callbacks_` is the `ActiveStream`, which calls `response_encoder_->encodeHeaders()` on the downstream HTTP/1.1 codec's `ResponseEncoderImpl`, serializing the response to the downstream TCP socket.\n\n### At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?\n\n| Phase | Filter Chain | Triggered by |\n|---|---|---|\n| Request headers arrive from downstream | **Decoder** | `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` via `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` |\n| Request body chunks from downstream | **Decoder** | `FilterManager::decodeData()` |\n| Request trailers from downstream | **Decoder** | `FilterManager::decodeTrailers()` |\n| Response headers arrive from upstream | **Encoder** | `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` via `UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge::decodeHeaders()` |\n| Response body chunks from upstream | **Encoder** | `FilterManager::encodeData()` |\n| Response trailers from upstream | **Encoder** | `FilterManager::encodeTrailers()` |\n\nThe decoder filter chain runs in configuration order (first-to-last). The encoder filter chain also runs in front-to-back order over `encoder_filters_`, but encoder filters are *prepended* during `createFilterChain()`, so effectively they execute in reverse configuration order (last-configured-first on response).\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Q1 Supporting Files\n\n- `source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.cc` \u2014 `TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()` (L56-126): socket accept loop, `cb_.onAccept()` call\n- `source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.h` \u2014 `TcpListenerImpl` class definition, listener accept load shedding\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc` \u2014 `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` (L80), `onAcceptWorker()` (L108), `newActiveConnection()` (L149)\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h` \u2014 `onSocketAccepted()` (L85): listener filter chain creation and execution\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc` \u2014 `continueFilterChain()` (L111), `newConnection()` (L185): filter iteration and redirect logic\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc` \u2014 `newConnection()` (L38): `findFilterChain()`, `createServerConnection()`, `createNetworkFilterChain()`\n- `source/common/network/listen_socket_impl.h` \u2014 `AcceptedSocketImpl` (L183): accepted socket wrapper\n\n### Q2 Supporting Files\n\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` \u2014 `onData()` (L486): codec creation and dispatch loop; Decoder filters are stored in `decoder_filters_` in configuration order.\n\nThen `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders(*request_headers_, end_stream)` (conn_manager_impl.cc:1439) is called, which dispatches to `FilterManager::decodeHeaders(nullptr, headers, end_stream)` (filter_manager.cc:537).\n\n`FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` iterates `decoder_filters_` from front to back (configuration order):\n\n```cpp\nfor (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    FilterHeadersStatus status = (*entry)->decodeHeaders(headers, (*entry)->end_stream_);\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n### What filter return values can stop or continue iteration?\n\nDecoder filter `decodeHeaders()` returns `FilterHeadersStatus`:\n\n| Return Value | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| `Continue` | Advance to the next decoder filter |\n| `StopIteration` | Stop; the filter must call `continueDecoding()` later to resume from the next filter |\n| `StopAllIterationAndBuffer` | Stop and buffer all subsequent data frames |\n| `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` | Stop and apply watermark-based buffering |\n| `ContinueAndDontEndStream` | Continue but suppress the `end_stream` flag to subsequent filters |\n\nHandled in `ActiveStreamFilterBase::commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback()` (filter_manager.cc:130). If `stoppedAll()` is true, iteration halts and resumes via `commonContinue()` (filter_manager.cc:50) when the filter calls `continueDecoding()`.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection\n\n### How does the router determine which route configuration to use?\n\nBefore calling `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders()`, `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` (conn_manager_impl.cc:1233-1244) snaps the route configuration:\n\n```cpp\nsnapped_route_config_ = connection_manager_.config_->routeConfigProvider()->configCast();\n```\n\nThis is an atomic snapshot of the current `RouteConfiguration` proto derived from static config or RDS. The `snapped_route_config_` is stored on the `ActiveStream` and passed to `refreshCachedRoute()` which calls `snapped_route_config_->route(request_headers, stream_info, random)`.\n\n### What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?\n\nInside the router filter `Filter::decodeHeaders()` (source/common/router/router.cc:445):\n\n1. `callbacks_->route()` returns the cached route (set earlier by `refreshCachedRoute()` in the HCM). The route config's `RouteImpl::matches()` evaluated all prefix/header/path matchers against the request.\n2. `route_->routeEntry()` returns the `RouteEntry` which holds the cluster name, timeout, retry policy, etc.\n3. `config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName())` (router.cc:519) fetches the `ThreadLocalCluster` from the cluster manager by name. Returns null if cluster does not exist (\u2192 503).\n4. `cluster_ = cluster->info()` stores the cluster's static metadata.\n\n### How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?\n\n```cpp\nauto host_selection_response = cluster->chooseHost(this);  // router.cc:664\n```\n\n`chooseHost()` delegates to the cluster's load balancer (Round Robin, Least Request, Random, Ring Hash, etc.). In the common synchronous path (no async host selection), it immediately returns a `HostConstSharedPtr`. If the returned host is null, `sendNoHealthyUpstreamResponse()` sends a 503.\n\n### What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?\n\nWith a valid host, `continueDecodeHeaders()` (router.cc:714) calls:\n\n```cpp\nstd::unique_ptr<GenericConnPool> generic_conn_pool = createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host);\n```\n\nThen an `UpstreamRequest` is created (router.cc:845) and immediately calls:\n\n```cpp\nconn_pool_->newStream(this);  // upstream_request.cc:404\n```\n\n`HttpConnPoolImplBase::newStream()` (conn_pool_base.cc:59-65) calls `newStreamImpl()` which:\n- If a ready (idle) client exists: attaches the stream immediately and fires `onPoolReady`.\n- Otherwise: creates a new TCP connection to the upstream host (via `ConnPoolImplBase::tryCreateNewConnections()`), queues the request as pending, and fires `onPoolReady` when the connection is established.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow\n\n### How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?\n\n`ConnPoolImplBase` (the base of all connection pools) manages three client lists: `ready_clients_`, `busy_clients_`, and `connecting_clients_`. When `newStreamImpl()` is called:\n\n1. If `ready_clients_` is non-empty, an idle client is taken and the stream is attached immediately via `attachStreamToClient()` \u2192 `onPoolReady()`.\n2. If no ready client exists, `tryCreateNewConnections()` initiates a new TCP connection to the upstream, creating a `CodecClient` (HTTP/1.1) or a multiplexed client (HTTP/2). The `PendingStream` is enqueued.\n3. When the TCP connection completes and the codec is initialized, the client moves to `ready_clients_` and the queued `PendingStream` is dispatched via `onPoolReady()`.\n\n`HttpConnPoolImplBase::onPoolReady()` (conn_pool_base.cc:84-93) calls:\n```cpp\nHttp::RequestEncoder& new_encoder = http_client->newStreamEncoder(response_decoder);\ncallbacks.onPoolReady(new_encoder, ...);\n```\n\nThis calls `UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady()` (upstream_request.cc:584), which stores `upstream_` (the `GenericUpstream`/`RequestEncoder`) and records connection timing in `StreamInfo`.\n\n### What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?\n\nThe last filter in the upstream HTTP filter chain is `UpstreamCodecFilter` (source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.cc). It is the terminal filter added by `DefaultUpstreamHttpFilterChainFactory` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:251-272).\n\nWhen headers have been processed by upstream filters, `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:52) is called:\n\n```cpp\nconst Http::Status status =\n    callbacks_->upstreamCallbacks()->upstream()->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n```\n\nFor HTTP/1.1, `upstream()` is a `Http1::RequestEncoderImpl` whose `encodeHeaders()` serializes the HTTP/1.1 request line and headers into a `Buffer` and writes to the upstream `Connection`.\n\nBody data follows via `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeData()` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:97) \u2192 `upstream()->encodeData()`.\n\nIf `onPoolReady` has not yet fired when `acceptHeadersFromRouter()` is called, `UpstreamCodecFilter` latches the headers in `latched_headers_` and waits. On `onUpstreamConnectionEstablished()` (upstream_codec_filter.cc:40), it replays `decodeHeaders()`.\n\n### How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?\n\nWhen the upstream sends a response, the upstream `CodecClient` (wrapping the upstream TCP connection) parses bytes using `ClientConnectionImpl`. The parsed response is delivered to `UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge` (the `ResponseDecoder` passed to `newStreamEncoder()`):\n\n- **`CodecBridge::decodeHeaders()`** (upstream_codec_filter.cc:147): calls `filter_.callbacks_->encodeHeaders(std::move(headers), end_stream, ...)` \u2014 this invokes `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` on the *downstream* filter manager, starting the encoder filter chain.\n- **`CodecBridge::decodeData()`** (upstream_codec_filter.cc:194): calls `filter_.callbacks_->encodeData(data, end_stream)` \u2192 `FilterManager::encodeData()`.\n- **`CodecBridge::decodeTrailers()`** (upstream_codec_filter.cc:200): calls `filter_.callbacks_->encodeTrailers()`.\n\n`FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (filter_manager.cc:1225) iterates `encoder_filters_` in front-to-back order (which corresponds to reverse configuration order, since encoder filters are prepended). Each filter gets to modify or stop the response. After all encoder filters pass, the response is written to the downstream socket via:\n\n```cpp\nfilter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders(headers, modified_end_stream);  // filter_manager.cc:1305\n```\n\n`filter_manager_callbacks_` is the `ActiveStream`, which calls `response_encoder_->encodeHeaders()` on the downstream HTTP/1.1 codec's `ResponseEncoderImpl`, serializing the response to the downstream TCP socket.\n\n### At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?\n\n| Phase | Filter Chain | Triggered by |\n|---|---|---|\n| Request headers arrive from downstream | **Decoder** | `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` via `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` |\n| Request body chunks from downstream | **Decoder** | `FilterManager::decodeData()` |\n| Request trailers from downstream | **Decoder** | `FilterManager::decodeTrailers()` |\n| Response headers arrive from upstream | **Encoder** | `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` via `UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge::decodeHeaders()` |\n| Response body chunks from upstream | **Encoder** | `FilterManager::encodeData()` |\n| Response trailers from upstream | **Encoder** | `FilterManager::encodeTrailers()` |\n\nThe decoder filter chain runs in configuration order (first-to-last). The encoder filter chain also runs in front-to-back order over `encoder_filters_`, but encoder filters are *prepended* during `createFilterChain()`, so effectively they execute in reverse configuration order (last-configured-first on response).\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Q1 Supporting Files\n\n- `source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.cc` \u2014 `TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()` (L56-126): socket accept loop, `cb_.onAccept()` call\n- `source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.h` \u2014 `TcpListenerImpl` class definition, listener accept load shedding\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc` \u2014 `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` (L80), `onAcceptWorker()` (L108), `newActiveConnection()` (L149)\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h` \u2014 `onSocketAccepted()` (L85): listener filter chain creation and execution\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc` \u2014 `continueFilterChain()` (L111), `newConnection()` (L185): filter iteration and redirect logic\n- `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc` \u2014 `newConnection()` (L38): `findFilterChain()`, `createServerConnection()`, `createNetworkFilterChain()`\n- `source/common/network/listen_socket_impl.h` \u2014 `AcceptedSocketImpl` (L183): accepted socket wrapper\n\n### Q2 Supporting Files\n\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` \u2014 `onData()` (L486): codec creation and dispatch loop; # Envoy Request Routing Flow

## Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

### Which component accepts the incoming TCP connection?

`TcpListenerImpl` (source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.cc) accepts the connection. During construction, it registers a level-triggered file event on the listening socket:

```cpp
socket_->ioHandle().initializeFileEvent(
    dispatcher, [this](uint32_t events) { return onSocketEvent(events); },
    Event::FileTriggerType::Level, Event::FileReadyType::Read);
```

When the event fires, `TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()` (tcp_listener_impl.cc:56) calls `socket_->ioHandle().accept()` to extract the peer socket, then wraps it in an `AcceptedSocketImpl` and calls `cb_.onAccept(std::make_unique<AcceptedSocketImpl>(...))` (tcp_listener_impl.cc:117).

The callback target is `ActiveTcpListener` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.h), which implements `Network::TcpListenerCallbacks`.

### How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?

After all listener filters run (see below), `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc:185) calls `listener_.newConnection(std::move(socket_), std::move(stream_info_))`.

Inside `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:38-76):

```cpp
const auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);
```

`findFilterChain()` matches against configured criteria such as destination IP/port, server name (SNI), transport protocol (set by the TLS inspector listener filter), and application protocol (set by the HTTP Inspector listener filter). The matching is hierarchical and the most-specific match wins.
